<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_17ac698c-46cf-44b6-b828-d1ed301d181d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<div id="review_1362560430" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1362560430" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1362560430?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1362560430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7171674031377689353"><br/><b>3.5 entertaining stars.</b> I like a sense of story progression from sequel to sequel when I embark into a series. I did not however detect that feeling when reading the second book in The Mediator series. Suze didn’t gain new abilities, she still made reckless moves (trusting one’s instinct is important, but there’s a limit not to cross), her relationships with secondary characters from the first volume didn’t change – or barely so – and the ending to the new ‘‘case’’ left me pretty darn confused a</span>
  <span id="freeText7171674031377689353" style="display:none"><br /><b>3.5 entertaining stars.</b> I like a sense of story progression from sequel to sequel when I embark into a series. I did not however detect that feeling when reading the second book in The Mediator series. Suze didn’t gain new abilities, she still made reckless moves (trusting one’s instinct is important, but there’s a limit not to cross), her relationships with secondary characters from the first volume didn’t change – or barely so – and the ending to the new ‘‘case’’ left me pretty darn confused and slightly frustrated. It hit me the same as if the author had used the ‘‘it was all just a dream’’ line. Yeah.<br /><br />BUT, it was an unexpected twist.<br /><br />AND, just like any other Meg Cabot book, this one was fun, well-written, atmospheric and engrossing!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7171674031377689353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer689324253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5881767859933608813"><br/><b>
  <blockquote>
<i>"You can't tell me you've </i>liked<i> being trapped in this room for a hundred and fifty years."<br/>"It hasn't been all bad," he said, with a smile. "Things have picked up recently."</i>
</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>Okayyyy sooooo I wasn't gong to write a review today, but it's going to be a long weekend (WOOT! Bring it on 4th of July!) and I know I will finish at LEAST one book and will need to post about it Tuesday-So I'd rather not get backlogged. Plus-<b>Any chance I get to boast about my Jesse and Suze addiction</b> to get people awar</span>
  <span id="freeText5881767859933608813" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <blockquote>
<i>"You can't tell me you've </i>liked<i> being trapped in this room for a hundred and fifty years."<br>"It hasn't been all bad," he said, with a smile. "Things have picked up recently."</i>
</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Okayyyy sooooo I wasn't gong to write a review today, but it's going to be a long weekend (WOOT! Bring it on 4th of July!) and I know I will finish at LEAST one book and will need to post about it Tuesday-So I'd rather not get backlogged. Plus-<b>Any chance I get to boast about my Jesse and Suze addiction</b> to get people aware of it again, <b>I'm going to do it</b>.<br><br>This is a series, I'm finding, that not only I liked, but many many of my friends did, too. Turns out? <b>I wasn't the only pre-teen laying in my bedroom binge-reading</b> this series and pining about Jesse like I thought I was....no wonder she is so popular. <i>Go figure</i>. It's so fun to talk to all you guys about how much we loved this and why it's still great, so that's why I feel the need to talk about each and every installment, no matter which are my favorite and which are just plain awesome (Pfft. They all are-even my least fav). <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Jesse has those kind of eyes some guys have, the kind of sad eyes that make you think you might want to try and make them not so sad.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I must say that I enjoyed the first installment more than this one, but I remember that being the case years and years ago when I first picked these up. I loved Suze's voice, again, and loved Jesse even more. But, as it is, I really wanted more Jesse. lol-I couldn't quite pinpoint why this one wasn't my favorite years ago, but now the BBF whore in me knows <i>exactly</i> why. There was plenty of Jesse, really, but OMG <b>is it too much to ask for him to be on <i>every</i> page</b>? Yes? Hmm. *pouts*<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Now that," he said, putting his hands down, "was your finest performance yet. You seemed caring, yet disgusted."<br>I glared at him. "Don't you," I asked, grumpily, "have some chains you're supposed to be rattling somewhere?"</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I actually found this one comical in the most subtle ways-the vampire aspect, <b>the dumb jock Suze attempts to tolerate</b>, the references to her monster-like poison ivy hands, the step-brother dynamic, and, frankly, Jesse's humor. I loved this book just like I knew I would, but <b>I love that I get the depth in which all the jokes are meant to be taken</b>. Before, yeah I laughed as a kid, but I certainly didn't realize just how wry the humor was-I mean, so refreshing. I even had forgotten about dear old Father Dominic-he and Suze's banter and relationship is something I had long since forgotten and I am so happy it's all coming back to me now-even stronger than before.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"A mediator is someone who <i>helps</i> others resolve conflicts. Not someone, who, er, kicks them in the face."<br>I smiled at him. "I'll keep that in mind," I said.<br>And I would, too. Right after I kicked Red's butt.<br>Whoever he was.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>So, yeah. I could go on and on about how happy these books make me, but I know for a fact they get better and better and <b>Jesse's jealousy gets stronger and stronger</b>....What's not to fall for?? So, with that being said, I think I'm going to leave the review here and <b>wish everyone a happy holiday weekend</b>. I wanted to pick the third up over the weekend after my fantasy, but I got granted an AMAZING ARC I did not expect to get, so I will probably pick it up first. But if I'm being honest? I already miss these guys. I have NO clue what the hell I'm going to do when I am done with these all over again. Probably cry. Yeah. Sounds about right. <br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea-peril-please-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287303i/17673713._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Twitter" href="https://twitter.com/starcrossedblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660580.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="RSS" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/starcrossedbookblog/METU" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660581.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="BLOGLOVIN" href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/star-crossed-book-blog-13035961" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>***********<br><br>Ahhh this series will NEVER get old. Never. What a refreshing reassurance. Jesse will literally never bore me....I guess that means I can re-read these yet again when I'm older. :P<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/8820746_zpsn0so3cpr.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer9927913558255106035"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Probably the weakest in the series but I had so much fun reading it nevertheless! I really like Meg's writing and she has a special place in my heart. She can write hilarious scenes but sad & relatable ones as well. But she does it in her own special way which I love. I feel like she captures Suze's development as a person (and mediator) fantastically. Oh, and Jesse is cutie as always.</span>

I feel like she captures Suze's development as a person (and mediator) fantastically. Oh, and Jesse is cutie as always.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2064748734624994500">Mini review:<br/><br/>I have been a fan of Meg Cabot since I was in high school. When I saw that this series was in my library I read the first book. And man was it fun! Curious about the second book I put it on hold. While yes Ninth Key was still entertaining the first book was better. <br/><br/>The beginning was a little to plot convenient.   <span id="freeText2064748734624994500" style="display:none">Mini review:<br /><br />I have been a fan of Meg Cabot since I was in high school. When I saw that this series was in my library I read the first book. And man was it fun! Curious about the second book I put it on hold. While yes Ninth Key was still entertaining the first book was better. <br /><br />The beginning was a little to plot convenient. It was a miscommunication that lead to a lot of consequences. I was hoping that Meg would train a bit more with Father Dom but that didn't happen. Jesse is still a mystery in this book.<br /><br />There are some things that are revealed. And as usual Suze was fun to read about! I enjoyed reading about her family. The ghost stuff was fun as well. I will definitely continue this series.<br /><br />I highly recommend this series!</span>

<div id="review_81743743" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81743743" />
    <a title="Io705" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3065936-io705"><img alt="Io705" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268686754p2/3065936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81743743?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Io705" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Io705" href="/user/show/3065936-io705">Io705</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81743743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14686506234271732335">The Ninth Key (Part Two of the Mediator Series)<br/>Final Response by Iolanthe Brooks<br/>12.24.09<br/><br/>I think Suze is just a confused girl trying to find her way. Only for her it’s even harder. Everyone is pressuring her to do different things, things a girl shouldn’t have to worry about. Her mom pressures her to go on dates, even if it means walking into traps and her mentor, Father Dominic, pressures her to help all these ghosts. If I were Suze, I’d be all confused inside.<br/>	<br/>Normal girls lean on each other wh</span>
  <span id="freeText14686506234271732335" style="display:none">The Ninth Key (Part Two of the Mediator Series)<br />Final Response by Iolanthe Brooks<br />12.24.09<br /><br />I think Suze is just a confused girl trying to find her way. Only for her it’s even harder. Everyone is pressuring her to do different things, things a girl shouldn’t have to worry about. Her mom pressures her to go on dates, even if it means walking into traps and her mentor, Father Dominic, pressures her to help all these ghosts. If I were Suze, I’d be all confused inside.<br />	<br />Normal girls lean on each other when they are going through tough times, but who can Suze lean on? No one understands her. It’s like she lost, and all alone in world where she doesn’t belong. But, what world is that? <br />	<br />I feel like maybe some people are just destined to not fit in. No matter how hard they try they’ll never be “right.” But, what if those people are the most kind, caring, sweet people? What happens? Can the sweetest of the sweetest endure being all alone? I don’t think they can. No one can, and just because these people are different from your average run-of-the-mill girl or boy, they’re still humans. And, no human can ever be all alone their whole life without going crazy. <br />	<br />I wonder if Suze is going to go crazy, I think she will. I think that Suze thinks that no one notices her, no one pays her any attention. So, she’s already started ruining her life by wearing shorter skirts and kissing random boys and hurting the ghosts instead of talking to them. Why would Suze let this happen to her? Why won't she just try to talk to the ghosts? <br /><br />Maybe she can’t bear to talk to them (the ghosts). It’s like all that peer pressure to be “normal” won’t let her talk to the ghosts. Maybe, she’s mad at them. Maybe she’s mad that they ruined her social life, that they hurt her, but did they?  Maybe the ghosts don’t have to ruin Suze’s life. Maybe they only ruin her life because she lets them. She lets everyone ruin her life. And, then I think she becomes to afraid to admit that she’s let people’s words hurt her, so she lies to herself. She tells herself that she’s some super strong ghost-buster (per-say) and that no one can hurt her. So she hurts the ghosts.<br />	<br />I think we all do this a lot, whether our ghosts are siblings or friends, or even mentors. We convince ourselves that we don’t need others love. And, then we take out all our pain on others. We let peer pressure make us crazy, so crazy that we could hurt and kill, and do beastly things. Instead of working things out, we choose to hurt each other. And, it’s a chain. We hurt one person and they hurt another and they hurt another, and it goes on and on and on. But, hurting others never solves anything. It just generates anger.<br />	<br />Suze is too stuck on what her mom says, on what others say, that she can’t even hear her heart over the roar of their words. She’s lost in a world of her mom’s dreams, and other’s dreams and commands. She’s just looking for a way to be herself, a mediator, but to also be happy and loved, and not alone. But, Suze is really stuck. By lying to herself she’s made almost impossible to get out of that cycle of hate. She refuses to admit to herself, that she’s not a grown-up. And, she can’t be a superhero. She can’t do everything right, because no one can. As soon as Suze can admit that she’s made mistakes, and that she always will, then she’ll be able to live as herself. She’ll be able to be happy being a mediator, not depressed. I think that if Suze will open her eyes she’ll be free.<br /><br />	But, no one said that was going to be easy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14686506234271732335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11442666142561806358">The Mediator series is definitely become one of my favorites. Perhaps it's too soon to say that since I've only read the first two books?   <span id="freeText11442666142561806358" style="display:none">The Mediator series is definitely become one of my favorites. Perhaps it's too soon to say that since I've only read the first two books? But I definitely like it.<br /><br />So, let's talk about Suze for a minute. This girl is everything I want to be. She's tough. She's sarcastic, and funny. She's relatable. She's just freaking awesome. I would want this girl as a friend. She's just a character I really clicked with. And that is a super rare occurrence. <br /><br />The thing I like about the Mediator books is you don't have to focus a lot. It's a nice, easy read and while I like books that are thought-provoking and deep, I also like when I can just relax with a book, when I can just effortlessly turn the pages. Not to say it's all fluff- the Mediator books do raise some interesting questions about the afterlife. But it's definitely a book that doesn't require you to clear your head and focus before reading.<br /><br />Jesse, Jesse, Jesse. He is both a fictional character AND dead. Simply painful. Why can't guys like him exist in the real world?? Or at least, at my school?? <br /><br />Overall, a book perfect for relaxing with on a Friday night. Five stars.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1379392603" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1379392603" />
    <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj"><img alt="Nasty Lady MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506395877p2/4026143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1379392603?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1379392603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17781352311215632029">This isn't necessary a bad book. But this book and the first book are always difficult for me to get into, compared with the rest of the series. Bryce and Tad are honestly sort of homogenous. At least with Michael (random guy who flirts with Suze in the third book) there's sort of a twist. It's still a decent book though, though I did think it was sort of lame Suze got grounded in the end. <br/><br/>To see review with gif click <a href='https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2015/09/04/ninth-key/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here.</a><br/><br/><br/>Original Reading Experience: <br/><br/>I read this in a binge read when I finally g</span>
  <span id="freeText17781352311215632029" style="display:none">This isn't necessary a bad book. But this book and the first book are always difficult for me to get into, compared with the rest of the series. Bryce and Tad are honestly sort of homogenous. At least with Michael (random guy who flirts with Suze in the third book) there's sort of a twist. It's still a decent book though, though I did think it was sort of lame Suze got grounded in the end. <br /><br />To see review with gif click <a href="https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2015/09/04/ninth-key/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br /><br />Original Reading Experience: <br /><br />I read this in a binge read when I finally got my hands on the rest of the series-I had read books five and then later four first BEFORE finally reading books one, two, and three.<br /><br />Honestly, I just wanted to get on with this one and get to the last book because I had to know how my ship was going to work out. Because it just had to because surely Meg wouldn’t be that cruel…<br /><br />Anyway, what I remembered the most about Ninth Key was Suze’s fashion choices-Armani sweater seat, Batgirl boots, and Betsey Johnson miniskirt. That outfit was imprinted on my brain.<br /><br /><br />And I kept thinking about it since. Or at least that’s the outfit I always associated Suze with besides the plethora of slip dresses that she wore in the fourth book.<br /><br />Funny, how this series became a lot of my fashion inspiration at the time. No Cosmo for me, but Mediator.<br /><br /><br />Reread:<br /><br />Ninth Key to me was always the forgotten book in the series. A lot of people say that about Reunion, but I actually like Reunion more or remember liking Reunion more-I think it Sleepy and Gina that made that one better than it really is.<br /><br />I so ship them. Despite the fact that Gina deserves someone a lot more responsible than Sleepy.<br /><br />Okay, all kidding aside, Ninth Key isn’t bad, it’s just not that remarkable.<br /><br />Well, the climax scenes were well done and hilarious, but besides them this book was a particular slow book. I have to give it Meg though for slowly developing the relationship between Suze and Jesse. I really do love a good slow burn romance, and this is what this one is. It’s such a arare thing in YA, so excuse me while I sort of relish in it.<br /><br />However, I don’t think there was really any growth between them in this installment other than Suze acknowledges that Jesse is hot, and Jesse interrupts a very awkward date with Tad.<br /><br />But we all knew it was never going to last with Tad. I’m sure he found himself a nice boyfriend when he moved to San Francisco, just saying. Honestly, Bryce and Suze were more believable and that’s pushing it.<br /><br />It’s odd how it takes Paul Slater, who is basically a sociopath, to actually be the one love interest that potentially can match Jesse and that’s mostly in fannon. Because Paul in cannon is sort of jerk, but he’s not in this book so we can’t talk about him.<br /><br />Boo.<br /><br />Most of the development to the overall series was done of the ancillary relationships-family and friends-which was nice. As I said before, it’s a filler book, but it does a good job showing how blended families relate to each other so that was good.<br /><br />And I liked how we got to see a bit more of Adam and CeeCee in this installment, though I did feel like they were used a bit by Suze.<br /><br />Bad Suze.<br /><br />Overall though, Ninth Key is a good quick read. It’s never going to have the same impact on me like other installments, but it doesn’t damper the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17781352311215632029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_241691971" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241691971" />
    <a title="Lubnaa (Romance Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library"><img alt="Lubnaa (Romance Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586826564p2/6095877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241691971?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lubnaa (Romance Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lubnaa (Romance Library)" href="/user/show/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library">Lubnaa (Romance Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library?shelf=interracial-couples">interracial-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241691971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5901876280757556147"><b>Re-read in 2020 on audio:</b><br/><br/>I don't know how Meg Cabot does it, but man, this series is just *chef's kiss* and it stands the test of time. Ninth Key pretty much takes place the following week after Shadowland. Just as Suze is beginning to adapt to her new school, a screaming ghost decides to visit her in the middle of the night while she is sleeping. Poor Suze 😂 But hey, at least she's got the hot ghost of Jesse de Silva keeping her company in her bedroom 😉 <br/><br/>The plot in this book is bigger than ever</span>
  <span id="freeText5901876280757556147" style="display:none"><b>Re-read in 2020 on audio:</b><br /><br />I don't know how Meg Cabot does it, but man, this series is just *chef's kiss* and it stands the test of time. Ninth Key pretty much takes place the following week after Shadowland. Just as Suze is beginning to adapt to her new school, a screaming ghost decides to visit her in the middle of the night while she is sleeping. Poor Suze 😂 But hey, at least she's got the hot ghost of Jesse de Silva keeping her company in her bedroom 😉 <br /><br />The plot in this book is bigger than ever, with Suze taking on a serial killing businessman. I love the way Meg Cabot builds up the plot. At first, Suze thinks it's just a regular mediating job and oh boy, was she wrong. I love how the author built up the creepiness of the Beaumonts. SO GOOD!! Suze is still a badass, if a reckless one. She is whip smart and uses her brain to get out of messy situations. We also have some great relationship development with Suze and David and also with Jesse and Suze. I vividly remember her fights with Jesse and I still enjoy them now LOL. And we finally got to meet her dad, who's been haunting her for years!<br /><br />As usual, Johanna Parker does an impeccable job narrating this book. She brings Suze to life and voices her character in the exact way I imagined her to be when I first read the series many years ago. Next book: it sounds like Gina will be paying Suze a visit! I honestly can't remember anything about it, so I'm excited to continue my re-read!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5901876280757556147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219895159" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19571418-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419269646p2/19571418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219895159?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/19571418-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330437387" href="/book/show/234908.High_Stakes">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219895159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13939455815652557711">High Stakes the second book in The Mediator series was okay but I think I preferred the first book. <br/><br/>Suzie was a little harsh at times in this book, especially towards her step brothers. She also tried to be funny at times but to me it seemed inappropriate, it just didn't really work for me. It made her seem pretty stupid to be honest. I expected her relationship with Jesse to progress a little in this book but it seems she is at a stand still with him. He saves her a lot but most of the time he </span>
  <span id="freeText13939455815652557711" style="display:none">High Stakes the second book in The Mediator series was okay but I think I preferred the first book. <br /><br />Suzie was a little harsh at times in this book, especially towards her step brothers. She also tried to be funny at times but to me it seemed inappropriate, it just didn't really work for me. It made her seem pretty stupid to be honest. I expected her relationship with Jesse to progress a little in this book but it seems she is at a stand still with him. He saves her a lot but most of the time he just disappears on her. <br /><br />The overall story line in this book was good and Cabot really has you guessing until the very last page. I changed my mind about who the bad guy was at least three times, the characters were quite unreliable in this book. <br /><br />I didn't like Tad though. He was stupid to not know what was going on with his dad and uncle. I also didn't understand why he was so interested in Suzie, it's not like they had anything in common. I don't think he will be in the next book, just like Bryce I think he will be a one off character. I hope that doesn't keep happening in this series, being introduced to boring love interests isn't good! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13939455815652557711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_350873205" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/350873205" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10303433-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506476466p2/10303433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/350873205?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/10303433-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10303433-megan?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10303433-megan?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10303433-megan?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350873205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17300751115173429312">Original rating: 4 stars<br/>7/2020 reread: 4 stars<br/><br/>-<blockquote>
  <i>I could give a seminar on five easy ways to kick a ghost's butt and not mess up your hair.</i>
</blockquote>Second volume! I managed to forget the plot of this book entirely, for some reason? Which is weird because it's actually quite distinct where its ghosts and mystery are concerned. In this volume, Suze is visited by a distraught spirit begging her to tell "Red" that he <i>didn't</i> kill her. With this limited information, Suze undertakes some amateur sleuthing, wh</span>
  <span id="freeText17300751115173429312" style="display:none">Original rating: 4 stars<br />7/2020 reread: 4 stars<br /><br />-<blockquote>
  <i>I could give a seminar on five easy ways to kick a ghost's butt and not mess up your hair.</i>
</blockquote>Second volume! I managed to forget the plot of this book entirely, for some reason? Which is weird because it's actually quite distinct where its ghosts and mystery are concerned. In this volume, Suze is visited by a distraught spirit begging her to tell "Red" that he <i>didn't</i> kill her. With this limited information, Suze undertakes some amateur sleuthing, which leads her to Thaddeus "Red" Beaumont, one of Salinas County's foremost real estate developers . . . and self-professed vampire. Oh, and she just so happens to be kinda-sorta-dating his son, Tad. <br /><br />I'm in the middle of my reread of book three as I write this, and <b>Ninth Key</b> works as an excellent bridge between the frenetic, simplistic, choppy style of <b>Shadowland</b> and the more refined, purposeful, incisive wit of <b>Reunion.</b> Prose, dialogue, pacing, and characterization all improved by several notches (a trend that will continue in book three). Additionally, the central mystery of this book (while no less raw than the previous conflict involving Heather Chambers) felt <i>cleaner</i>. More mature, if you will. Not only because the writing is smoother but because the Beaumont's dirty laundry has a great ecopolitical bent, replete with humor-veiled indictments of corporate greed, urban sprawl, and irresponsible wealth. <br /><br />I'm still really impressed by how serious the conflicts in <b>The Mediator</b> series have been. These books pass themselves off as fairly frivolous YA titles, but their content can be fucking dark, man. <b>Shadowland</b> dealt with the furious ghost of a mentally-ill teenage girl who killed herself during an emotional episode, ending with an <i>exorcism</i> of said girl, and <b>Ninth Key</b> somehow only raised those stakes (ha ha) by presenting dangerous, powerful adult men as the installment's antagonists. The scenes where the killer describes his plan to dispose of Suze, thus silencing her, are actually pretty graphic. <br /><br />Not to mention, the closure we receive with the original ghost--the distraught woman begging Suze to tell Red he didn't kill her--becomes touchingly personal, also covering some heavy subjects (such as major end-of-life decisions and the impact this might have on surviving family members). <br /><br />Idk, the subject matter is always so much more mature than I expect, and I think that's part of what makes these books really special. Suze is a mediator, meaning she deals frequently with the restless spirits of the dead. And this series doesn't shy away from presenting these spirits in a realistic, human light. These are people who died of wasting disease (while young, middle-aged, or old), by murder, by suicide, by accident, etc. The seriousness of these ghosts' afflictions adds such understated weight to the narrative, and it really contextualizes Suze as a character. Jesse as well--that scene where he describes the killer's "bedevilment" was straight up savage.<blockquote>
  <i>But I really hate it when I cry. I'd much rather bleed or throw up or something.</i>
</blockquote>As for Suze and Jesse, their relationship makes nice strides in this second novel. The attraction between them is definitely apparent: Suze begins to joke about other romantic interests not comparing to him (still in a very offhand, tongue-in-cheek manner), and Jesse displays the first indication of romantic attachment via jealousy disguised as prim, brotherly concern (something we'll see a whole hell of a lot more of in <b>Haunted</b>).<blockquote>
  <i>Jesse has those kind of eyes some guys have, the kind of sad eyes that make you think you might want to try and make them not so sad. That's why I have to make a point of being so mean to him. I'm pretty sure there's a rule against that. I mean, in Father Dom's mediation guidelines. About mediators and ghosts getting together, and trying to, um, cheer each other up. If you know what I mean.</i>
</blockquote> Suze won't reach a point of unrequited yearning until book four, roughly, which aligns well with the timeline of their friendship, too. I still really enjoy the development and pacing of their interactions. It helps that Suze always has such serious shit going on--she's always <b>doing</b> something that doesn't involve Jesse at all, usually. He pretty much just pops up to give some ghost-advice or to lend a hand during a major conflict. <br /><br />We don't learn much more about Jesse's history in this book--again, we won't until book four. This builds up such suspense and excitement as book after book passes, each plot centering around a different ghost or ghosts, multiple--and <b>none of them</b> about the most important ghost in the entire series, and one of the main characters, who remains deliciously enigmatic for three full novels. Even knowing what happened to him, I'm still sitting here like, <i>Jesse was murdered. <b>Murdered</b>! Somebody killed this gentle, intelligent, warm person. Why isn't anybody talking about that? Why isn't Suze digging up this fucking dirt!? I can't take it anymore!</i><br /><br />Of course, Jesse's story-line takes center stage during books four and six, especially, and it's all the more dramatic and heartrending for the wait. <br /><br />For negatives: Of course, the series hasn't hit its full stride yet with its prose and characterization, as mentioned above. Some of the scenes with the killer at the end felt highly scripted, a bit too convenient and deliberately set-up to make Suze appear to be as supremely badass as possible. I would have liked to see Suze really get freaked during those scenes, as I think would have been more natural considering the extreme danger she found herself in.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17300751115173429312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_153271346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153271346" />
    <a title="Reading Vacation" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5102733-reading-vacation"><img alt="Reading Vacation" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341857406p2/5102733.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153271346?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Vacation" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Vacation" href="/user/show/5102733-reading-vacation">Reading Vacation</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153271346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3174733016812626347">REVIEW<br/><br/>A triple decker review. This is what you end up with when a series is so good that you read the books one right after the other. <br/><br/>In Ninth Key, Suze spends a good part of her time trying to figure out if Tad Beaumont (aka Red) is responsible for a murder. While the interactions between Suze and Tad were nice, I was much more drawn to the scenes with Suze and Jesse. Remember Jesse, he’s the ghost who lives in Suze’s room. Less Red and more Jesse! There are some completely unexpected twists t</span>
  <span id="freeText3174733016812626347" style="display:none">REVIEW<br /><br />A triple decker review. This is what you end up with when a series is so good that you read the books one right after the other. <br /><br />In Ninth Key, Suze spends a good part of her time trying to figure out if Tad Beaumont (aka Red) is responsible for a murder. While the interactions between Suze and Tad were nice, I was much more drawn to the scenes with Suze and Jesse. Remember Jesse, he’s the ghost who lives in Suze’s room. Less Red and more Jesse! There are some completely unexpected twists to the plot and I LOVED the way Meg Cabot worked them in. She is a genius at writing a mystery. GENIUS.<br /><br />Reunion is my favorite Mediator book of the series so far. In this book, Suze is caught between the ghosts of four teens who died in a car accident (the RLS Angels) and Michael, the boy from her school who the ghosts are blaming for their deaths. It’s an all-out war as the ghosts are trying to get revenge on Michael. There is no shortage of action and I liked that the car accident plot was so realistic. Even with ghosts being involved, the plot felt very REAL.<br /><br />In Darkest Hour, Suze comes face-to-face with Maria, the ghost who was engaged to her beloved Jesse. Since I am so into the relationship between Suze and Jesse, I was really excited to read about Jesse’s former fiancé. The most romantic of the series so far, Darkest Hour will tug at your heart. Be prepared for a little side-plot action with the little boy Suze is babysitting – his name is Jack and he’s an eight-year-old mediator. I really enjoy how Meg Cabot put awesome little gems like this into her stories. <br /><br />It’s easy to see that I love the Mediator series. I can’t wait to read Haunted (book 5) and Twilight (book 6). <br /><br />RATING<br /><br />5 Plot<br /><br />4 Characters<br /><br />5 Attention Grabbing<br /><br />5 Girlie Meter<br /><br />4 Ending<br /><br /><br />23 TOTAL<br /><br /><br />5 STARS</span>
  <a data-text-id="3174733016812626347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_998620518" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/998620518" />
    <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd"><img alt="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382576238p2/8096484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/998620518?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd">Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=harper">harper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=pov-girl">pov-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=i-read-a-book-and-i-liked-it-3-star">i-read-a-book-and-i-liked-it-3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=covers-blueness">covers-blueness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=read-multiple-book-series-by-author">read-multiple-book-series-by-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=series-books">series-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=book-series-that-are-over-with">book-series-that-are-over-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=signed-copy">signed-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer998620518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15243934742394442095">This and other reviews can be found on <a href='http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Psychotic Nerd</a><br/><br/><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br/>I read the first book a few months ago and I enjoyed it! This isn't a dark ghost story, more of the fun variety, and it has a common plot, but I enjoyed it!<br/><br/>Suz is trying to be semi normal, but the fact that there's a mediator prevents that. Again. This time she's woken by a screaming woman, a ghost, who needs Suz to tell "Red" that he didn't kill her. Suz has no idea who this "Red" is, so she asks around. Turns out "Red" is </span>
  <span id="freeText15243934742394442095" style="display:none">This and other reviews can be found on <a href="http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Psychotic Nerd</a><br /><br /><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br />I read the first book a few months ago and I enjoyed it! This isn't a dark ghost story, more of the fun variety, and it has a common plot, but I enjoyed it!<br /><br />Suz is trying to be semi normal, but the fact that there's a mediator prevents that. Again. This time she's woken by a screaming woman, a ghost, who needs Suz to tell "Red" that he didn't kill her. Suz has no idea who this "Red" is, so she asks around. Turns out "Red" is the nickname of Tad Beaumont's dad. Suz ends up much deeper when the billionaire dad could be making people "disappear". And possibly insane. On the brightside, Suz is now dating Tad Beaumont, the hottest guy in school. <br /><br />From what I understand, based on other reviews, this isn't the best book in the series, but it's still good. Suz is a very great narrator. She's very spunky and I absolutely love her sarcastic voice! This book gets really, uh, messed up as it goes on, which is why I have odd feelings towards it. It actually takes an oddly dark turn, but also doesn't feel as serious. This book has a wholly fun vibe to it, even when things get dark, for some odd reason.<br /><br />There is a love interest, per say, in this book. But it never really goes anywhere and it also takes a back seat to everything else. Tad, the love interest, was really boring and kind of dumb. Suz says herself in the book that the only thing she really likes about him is his looks. Honestly, Tad's just there because of the plot and because Suz can't be with Jesse.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>IN CONCLUSION</u>
</b><br />All in all, this was a fun book! These books are really quick and easy reads! I have all of them sitting on my shelf ready for me to read, so I'll be binge reading the rest of them soon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15243934742394442095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZX5DTfo1OVlkmegY81CtiGTXrEkngudOvTN3n0MSFLLUd4LtGLuCcg8U7aKYLQApZuBMNjIOlVJnjvvJVL/hsA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bTerw0940qZhYB0T5N341BuUEt2YqcfT8d/SIp0/SvHcPmpjrfZpjQrtGKmPoFV1GaPyoo0ltc8rYl50ipK/8w==')})
  }
//]]>

But you can’t take the darkness out of the boy.\n\nAll Susannah Simon wants is to make a good impression at her first job since graduating from college (and since becoming engaged to Dr. Jesse de Silva). But when she’s hired as a guidance counselor at her alma mater, she stumbles across a decade-old murder, and soon ancient history isn’t all that’s coming back to haunt her. Old ghosts as well as new ones are coming out of the woodwork, some to test her, some to vex her, and it isn’t only because she’s a mediator, gifted with second sight. \n\nWhat happens when old ghosts come back to haunt you?\n\nIf you’re a mediator, you might have to kick a little ass.\n\nFrom a sophomore haunted by the murderous specter of a child to ghosts of a very different kind—including Paul Slater, Suze’s ex, who shows up to make a bargain Suze is certain must have come from the Devil himself—Suze isn’t sure she’ll make it through the semester, let alone to her wedding night. Suze is used to striking first and asking questions later. But what happens when ghosts from her past—including one she found nearly impossible to resist—strike first?<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"15993574086138382329\" href=\"#\" This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
